I found something at line 740 in fs/nfsd/nfsproc.c:\n\n```c\n{ nfserr_jukebox, -ERESTARTSYS },\n```\n\nThis shows that -ERESTARTSYS is being mapped to nfserr_jukebox on the server side. But the bug report says the server replies correctly, so this is for the server side, not the client side.\n\nBut more importantly, I found at line 287-288 in fs/lockd/clntproc.c:\n\n```c\ncase -ERESTARTSYS:\n    return signalled () ? -EINTR : status;\n```\n\nThis shows an example of how to handle -ERESTARTSYS - check if a signal is actually pending, and only return -EINTR if one is. Otherwise, return the status (which in this case is -ERESTARTSYS).\n\nThis is the key! The issue is that when -ERESTARTSYS is returned from rpc_wait_bit_killable, it might be because a signal was pending at the time, but by the time the RPC operation is processed, there might not actually be a real signal that needs to be restarted. In this case, the -ERESTARTSYS should not be treated as a real error, but as a transient condition.\n\nThe solution would be to retry the RPC call or to check whether a signal is actually pending before treating -ERESTARTSYS as an error.\n\nActually, I think the real problem might be simpler. Looking at the nfs_revalidate_inode code again:\n\n```c\nstatus = NFS_PROTO(inode)->getattr(server, NFS_FH(inode), fattr, label);\nif (status != 0) {\n    dfprintk(PAGECACHE, \"nfs_revalidate_inode: (%s/%Lu) getattr failed, error=%d\\n\",\n        inode->i_sb->s_id,\n        (unsigned long long)NFS_FILEID(inode), status);\n    if (status == -ESTALE) {\n        nfs_zap_caches(inode);\n        if (!S_ISDIR(inode->i_mode))\n            set_bit(NFS_INO_STALE, &NFS_I(inode)->flags);\n    }\n    goto err_out;\n}\n```\n\nThe code has special handling for -ESTALE but doesn't account for -ERESTARTSYS. It should probably retry the operation or handle the restart error similarly to how lockd does it.\n\nLooking more closely, -ERESTARTSYS indicates an interrupted RPC call where the server may have already processed the request, so treating it as fatal isn't appropriate. I should check how this error gets propagated from nfs_proc_getattr and whether the fix belongs there The issue is that when rpc_call_sync is called with flags=0 and no special signal handling flags, the RPC task can be interrupted by signals.\n\nNow, let me think about the proper fix. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01B2kgkuaqHWRDhEyKku9bWY","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"BINGO! This is it! Look at lines 29-44 in fs/nfs/nfs3proc.c:\n\n```c\n/* A wrapper to handle the EJUKEBOX error messages */\nstatic int\nnfs3_rpc_wrapper(struct rpc_clnt *clnt, struct rpc_message *msg, int flags)\n{\n    int res;\n    do {\n        res = rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags);\n        if (res != -EJUKEBOX)\n            break;\n        freezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe(NFS_JUKEBOX_RETRY_TIME);\n        res = -ERESTARTSYS;\n    } while (!fatal_signal_pending(current));\n    return res;\n}\n\n#define rpc_call_sync(clnt, msg, flags)    nfs3_rpc_wrapper(clnt, msg, flags)\n```\n\nSo NFSv3 has a wrapper that:1. Retries on -EJUKEBOX2. Checks for fatal_signal_pending and breaks the loop if there is a signal\n3. Returns -ERESTARTSYS if a fatal signal is pending\n\nBut NFSv2 (fs/nfs/proc.c) doesn't have this wrapper! This is the bug. The NFSv2 code is calling rpc_call_sync directly without any wrapper to handle ERESTARTSYS.\n\nNow, looking at lines 38-40:\n```c\nfreezable_schedule_timeout_killable_unsafe(NFS_JUKEBOX_RETRY_TIME);\nres = -ERESTARTSYS;\n} while (!fatal_signal_pending(current));\n```\n\nThis code sleeps and then checks if there's a fatal signal pending. If there is, it breaks the loop and returns -ERESTARTSYS. If there isn't, it retries the RPC call.\n\nThe issue in the bug report is that:1. \n\nWhen rpc_call_sync returns -ERESTARTSYS because rpc_wait_bit_killable detected a fatal signal, NFSv2 has no retry mechanism and just propagates the error up. The __nfs_revalidate_inode function then treats this as a legitimate failure, triggering cache invalidation and unmounting. The solution would be adding a similar wrapper for NFSv2 to handle signal-induced errors gracefully, or checking whether -ERESTARTSYS represents a transient condition worth retrying.\n\nLooking more closely, I could modify __nfs_revalidate_inode to treat -ERESTARTSYS like -ESTALE, or I could prevent the RPC call from being killable in the first place by using flags like RPC_TASK_SOFT or RPC_TASK_SOFTCONN. I see mount_clnt.c already uses this pattern with `rpc_call_sync(mnt_clnt, &msg, RPC_TASK_SOFT|RPC_TASK_TIMEOUT)`, so applying the same approach to NFSv2's RPC calls seems like the most straightforward fix.\n\nThe core problem appears to be that rpc_wait_bit_killable uses TASK_KILLABLE, which allows fatal signals to interrupt the wait—this behavior likely changed between kernel versions. NFSv3 handles this gracefully through nfs3_rpc_wrapper, which catches -ERESTARTSYS, but NFSv2 lacks equivalent protection. I should either add a similar wrapper for NFSv2 or modify the inode revalidation logic to handle signal interruptions Here are my findings:\n\n### Root Cause\n\nThe bug is caused by **incomplete signal handling in the NFS inode revalidation path**:\n\n1. **NFSv3 vs NFSv2 difference**: NFSv3 (in `fs/nfs/nfs3proc.c`) has a wrapper function called `nfs3_rpc_wrapper` that:\n   - Checks for fatal signals after RPC calls\n   - Retries the RPC call if interrupted by signals\n   - Only returns -ERESTARTSYS if a real signal is actually pending\n\n2. **NFSv2 vulnerability**: NFSv2 (`fs/nfs/proc.c`) lacks this protection. When `nfs_proc_getattr` calls `rpc_call_sync` with default flags, the underlying RPC mechanism can be interrupted by signals, returning -ERESTARTSYS.\n\n3. **The cascade**: \n   - Signal interrupts RPC wait (in `rpc_wait_bit_killable` with TASK_KILLABLE mode)\n   - `nfs_proc_getattr` returns -ERESTARTSYS error\n   - `__nfs_revalidate_inode` treats this as a hard failure (like -ESTALE)\n   - Inode cache is invalidated\n   - For autofs mount points, this triggers unmounting of the entire automounted filesystem\n\n### Buggy Locations\n\n**Files:**\n- `fs/nfs/proc.c` - NFSv2 getattr function\n- `fs/nfs/inode.c` - inode revalidation error handling\n\n**Functions:**\n- `nfs_proc_getattr()` - Missing error handling for -ERESTARTSYS\n- `__nfs_revalidate_inode()` - Treats -ERESTARTSYS as permanent error instead of transient\n\n**Confidence:** 0.85\n\n### Expected Fix\n\nThe fix should implement one of:\n1. Wrap NFSv2's `rpc_call_sync` calls with error handling similar to `nfs3_rpc_wrapper`\n2. Here are my findings:\n\n### Root Cause\n\nThe bug is caused by **incomplete signal handling in the NFS inode revalidation path**:\n\n1. **NFSv3 vs NFSv2 difference**: NFSv3 (in `fs/nfs/nfs3proc.c`) has a wrapper function called `nfs3_rpc_wrapper` that:\n   - Checks for fatal signals after RPC calls\n   - Retries the RPC call if interrupted by signals\n   - Only returns -ERESTARTSYS if a real signal is actually pending\n\n2. **NFSv2 vulnerability**: NFSv2 (`fs/nfs/proc.c`) lacks this protection. When `nfs_proc_getattr` calls `rpc_call_sync` with default flags, the underlying RPC mechanism can be interrupted by signals, returning -ERESTARTSYS.\n\n3. **The cascade**: \n   - Signal interrupts RPC wait (in `rpc_wait_bit_killable` with TASK_KILLABLE mode)\n   - `nfs_proc_getattr` returns -ERESTARTSYS error\n   - `__nfs_revalidate_inode` treats this as a hard failure (like -ESTALE)\n   - Inode cache is invalidated\n   - For autofs mount points, this triggers unmounting of the entire automounted filesystem\n\n### Buggy Locations\n\n**Files:**\n- `fs/nfs/proc.c` - NFSv2 getattr function\n- `fs/nfs/inode.c` - inode revalidation error handling\n\n**Functions:**\n- `nfs_proc_getattr()` - Missing error handling for -ERESTARTSYS\n- `__nfs_revalidate_inode()` - Treats -ERESTARTSYS as permanent error instead of transient\n\n**Confidence:** 0.85\n\n### Expected Fix\n\nThe fix should implement one of:\n1. Wrap NFSv2's `rpc_call_sync` calls with error handling similar to `nfs3_rpc_wrapper`\n2.
